   1: ## Code Review Report: `staffordersmobile.jsx`
   2: 
   3: ### Scope
   4: - Reviewed source: `C:\Dev\worktrees\task-260414-065351\pages\StaffOrdersMobile\staffordersmobile.jsx`
   5: - Context read: `StaffOrdersMobile README.md`, `BUGS.md`
   6: - Artifacts are stored in `C:\Dev\menuapp-code-review\pages\StaffOrdersMobile\` because the reviewed worktree is outside the writable workspace roots.
   7: 
   8: ### Summary
   9: The file still has several live regressions against issues already tracked in `BUGS.md`, plus a few structural problems around data scoping, i18n, and request/favorites handling. I did not find a fresh P0 crash/data-loss bug, but there are multiple P1 issues that can block staff workflows or show incorrect data.
  10: 
  11: ### Critical Issues (P0) â€” Must Fix
  12: - No new P0 issue confirmed from this pass.
  13: 
  14: ### High Priority (P1) â€” Should Fix
  15: - [P1] Any `StaffAccessLink` write can incorrectly replace the whole page with `BindingScreen` - `gateView` treats `updateLinkMutation.isPending` as equivalent to device binding (`staffordersmobile.jsx:3262-3265`), but the same mutation object is also used for favorites, cabinet auto-bind, and logout unbind (`3051-3067`, `3072-3086`, `3097-3105`, `3225-3230`). In token mode, a normal favorite toggle can blank the UI behind a fake binding screen. FIX: split device binding into a dedicated mutation, or gate `BindingScreen` only on `tokenState === "bind_needed"` plus a dedicated bind-in-flight flag.
  16: 
  17: - [P1] Logout unbind race regression is back - `handleLogout` fires `updateLinkMutation.mutate(...)` and immediately clears local state and redirects after 500 ms (`3225-3237`). If the update is slow or fails, the old device can remain bound and the token link stays locked to the current device. `BUGS.md` already records this as a fixed bug. FIX: make logout async, `await` the `StaffAccessLink.update`, handle failure explicitly, and redirect only after the unbind finishes or the user confirms a fallback.
  18: 
  19: - [P1] Served-orders section is not scoped to the active table session - `servedOrders` is fetched only by `{ table: group.id, status: "served" }` (`1776-1779`). On a reused table, served dishes from a previous session can leak into the current card, which matches the stale-session failure mode documented in the README/BUGS notes. FIX: filter served orders by the current `table_session` (or at minimum by current shift + open session) instead of table ID alone.
  20: 
  21: - [P1] Ungrouped request cards still bypass the accepted/assignee step - the standalone `RequestCard` action sends `new -> in_progress` directly (`4324`) and never writes `assignee` / `assigned_at`. That contradicts the two-step request flow restored elsewhere in this file and can leave non-table requests without ownership tracking. FIX: align `RequestCard` with the table-request flow: `new/open -> accepted` with assignee metadata, then `accepted -> done`.
  22: 
  23: - [P1] Restaurant scoping is lost when `partnerId` is missing - non-token users with role `admin` are allowed through `gateView` (`3283-3297`), and the page then falls back to global `.list()` queries for tables, orders, and service requests (`3333-3336`, `3460`, `3482`). That breaks the page contract described in the README and can expose cross-restaurant operational data in a restaurant-specific staff screen. FIX: require a restaurant/partner context for every non-token entry path, or disable all queries when `partnerId` is missing instead of falling back to global lists.
  24: 
  25: - [P1] The page is still broadly non-compliant with Base44 i18n rules - `useI18n()` is only used for stage-name translation (`2839`), while most user-facing copy is hardcoded in constants and JSX (`213-349`, `2389-2451`, `2475-2581`, `4165-4465`). There are also hardcoded fallbacks such as `partnerData?.name || "Ð ÐµÑÑ‚Ð¾Ñ€Ð°Ð½"` (`3327`) and `staffName || "Ð¡Ð¾Ñ‚Ñ€ÑƒÐ´Ð½Ð¸Ðº"` (`2506`). FIX: move all user-visible strings, labels, placeholders, ARIA text, toasts, and fallback copy to `t('page.section.key')`, and convert text arrays/constants into helpers that receive `t`.
  26: 
  27: ### Medium Priority (P2) â€” Recommended
  28: - [P2] Favorites storage mixes table favorites and request favorites, but the "My Tables" UI treats them as one bucket - request favorites are stored with the same `favorites` array as table favorites (`1525-1528`, `3072-3089`), while the My Tables modal and profile sheet count `favorites.length` and `clearAllFavorites()` wipes the entire array (`2389-2390`, `2451`, `2532-2535`, `3097-3108`). Clearing "my tables" also clears starred requests. FIX: separate table and request favorites logically, or derive `tableFavorites` / `requestFavorites` before counting and clearing.
  29: 
  30: - [P2] Favorite lookup does not normalize IDs on read - writes normalize IDs through `getLinkId()` (`3072-3075`), but `isFavorite` compares the raw `id` directly (`3093-3095`). If Base44 returns numeric IDs or link objects, stars can disappear or fail to match persisted favorites. FIX: normalize `id` inside `isFavorite` the same way as `toggleFavorite`.
  31: 
  32: - [P2] The double-`Ð¡Ñ‚Ð¾Ð»` regression is present in multiple live surfaces - the file still hardcodes `Ð¡Ñ‚Ð¾Ð» ${name}` in request cards (`1512`), single-order cards (`1616-1618`), and the My Tables modal (`2431`). `BUGS.md` already tracks this exact regression family. If table names already include the prefix in the DB, the UI shows `Ð¡Ñ‚Ð¾Ð» Ð¡Ñ‚Ð¾Ð» 22`. FIX: reuse one guarded helper such as `withTablePrefix()` / `stripTablePrefix()` everywhere a table label is built.
  33: 
  34: - [P2] Shift parsing can still return `NaN` and poison the shift filter - `parseTime` in `getShiftStartTime()` just splits and multiplies (`848-851`) and no longer guards `isNaN(h) || isNaN(m)`. That regression can produce invalid shift-start dates from bad `working_hours`, which then corrupts order/request filtering. `BUGS.md` lists this as previously fixed. FIX: restore the `NaN` guard and return `null` for malformed times before computing the shift start.
  35: 
  36: - [P2] `AudioContext` cleanup regression is back - `createBeep()` allocates an `AudioContext` (`1020-1043`) and mount code stores it in `audioRef` (`2925-2933`), but there is no unmount cleanup that closes `audioRef.current.ctx`. `BUGS.md` already records this leak as fixed once. FIX: add a cleanup `useEffect` that closes the context on unmount and nulls the ref.
  37: 
  38: - [P2] Most mutations still swallow non-rate-limit failures - order mutations in `OrderCard` and `OrderGroupCard` only roll back cache and never surface an error (`1576-1588`, `1882-1897`); the request mutation only handles rate limits and ignores other failures (`3513-3521`). On a failed update, the optimistic UI can revert with no explanation to the waiter. FIX: add user-visible error feedback for all mutation failures and funnel rate-limit failures into the same handling path.
  39: 
  40: - [P2] Request assignee checks are not normalized - the requests section uses `request.assignee === effectiveUserId` (`2333`) even though the rest of the file normalizes Base44 link fields with `getLinkId()`. If `request.assignee` is an object/value-link, the assignee pill never appears and "assigned to me" logic is wrong. FIX: compare `getLinkId(request.assignee)` to `effectiveUserId`.
  41: 
  42: ### Low Priority (P3) â€” Nice to Have
  43: - [P3] Production debug logging is still present - the session cleanup effect prints to `console.log` on success and failure (`2943-2951`). Project rules explicitly call out console logging as a production violation. FIX: remove the logs or route them through a controlled debug/logger flag that is off in production.
  44: 
  45: - [P3] Sort-mode radios can fire the handler twice per tap - each sort option binds `onClick` on the wrapping `<label>` and `onChange` on the nested `<input>` (`2675-2681`, `2698-2704`). A single tap can therefore call `onChangeSortMode()` twice, causing duplicate toasts and duplicate writes. FIX: keep the handler in one place only, preferably the radio `onChange`.

1693: function pluralRu(n, one, few, many) {
1694:   const abs = Math.abs(n) % 100;
1695:   const last = abs % 10;
1696:   if (abs > 10 && abs < 20) return many;
1697:   if (last > 1 && last < 5) return few;
1698:   if (last === 1) return one;
1699:   return many;
1700: }

+# Review: SOM-BUG-S270-01 KS Prompt
+
+Date: 2026-04-14
+Target: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx` (4538 lines)
+Context: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/BUGS.md`
+
+## Scope note
+
+I did not find a separate raw prompt file in the repository. This review validates the draft proposal as described by these checks:
+
+1. 5 fan-out locations
+2. `runBatchSequential` helper
+3. invalidate-once optimization
+4. `120ms` delay
+5. missing fan-out locations
+6. `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync`
+
+## Summary
+
+The draft direction is mostly right at the problem level: the current file does have real burst-update paths, and the reported `429` after "Выдать все" is credible from the live code. The main prompt risk is implementation precision. In this file, some candidate anchors are dead commented code, the actual order fan-out is centralized in one shared helper, and `mutateAsync` alone does not remove per-item invalidations because the mutation callbacks still fire on every call.
+
+## Findings
+
+### [P1] Invalidate-once is not sound if the prompt only switches loops to `mutateAsync`
+
+- `advanceMutation` still invalidates on every mutation settle at `1882-1897`:
+  - `1895`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["orders"] });`
+  - `1896`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["servedOrders", group.id] });`
+- `updateRequestMutation` still invalidates on every success at `3513-3521`:
+  - `3515`: `onSuccess: () => queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["serviceRequests"] }),`
+- `mutateAsync()` changes call shape, not mutation lifecycle. If the prompt says "use `mutateAsync` sequentially, then invalidate once after the loop", that is incomplete. The per-item `onSettled` / `onSuccess` handlers will still refetch unless the mutation callbacks are taught to skip invalidation during batch mode.
+
+Additional request-specific caveat:
+
+- `updateRequestMutation.mutationFn` currently spreads every non-`id` field into the entity update at `3514`.
+- Any batch-only flag such as `skipInvalidate`, `batch`, or `silent` would be written into `ServiceRequest` unless explicitly stripped there.
+
+### [P1] Global `onCloseRequest: mutate -> mutateAsync` is not a drop-in safe change
+
+- Parent wiring is currently synchronous at `4399`:
+  - `onCloseRequest={(reqId, newStatus, extraFields) => updateRequestMutation.mutate({ id: reqId, status: newStatus, ...extraFields })}`
+- Single-row request buttons call `onCloseRequest(...)` without awaiting or catching:
+  - live detail-view request actions are embedded on `2333`
+  - older mirrors at `658` and `1273` are inside block comments, not live
+- If `4399` is changed to `mutateAsync(...)`, those handlers start returning promises. On failure, that can produce unhandled promise rejections unless every caller does `await` with `try/catch`, or explicitly uses `void ...catch(...)`.
+
+Safer prompt direction:
+
+- keep the existing sync `onCloseRequest` for one-off button clicks
+- add a separate async batch-specific helper / prop for bulk request actions
+
+### [P1] The prompt must distinguish live fan-out points from dead commented duplicates
+
+There are two large commented-out render snapshots:
+
+- `546-785`
+- `1148-1418`
+
+That matters because several older bulk-action anchors inside those blocks are not live:
+
+- request bulk bar at `639`
+- request bulk bar at `1254`
+- bulk order buttons at `671`, `694`, `709`, `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+The only live request bulk fan-out is the detail-view bulk bar embedded on `2333`, where:
+
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "accept all"
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "serve all"
+
+### [P2] The real order fan-out is centralized at `1956-1965`, not at the three bulk button lines
+
+Live table-card bulk entry points are real:
+
+- `2335`: bulk action for `newOrders`
+- `2337`: bulk action for `inProgressSections`
+- `2339`: bulk action for `readyOrders`
+
+But those three buttons all funnel into one actual mutation fan-out:
+
+- `1956-1965`: `handleOrdersAction`
+- `1960-1962`: `actionable.forEach(... advanceMutation.mutate(...))`
+
+If the prompt only lists `2335/2337/2339`, the implementor can easily patch button call sites and miss the shared loop that actually creates the burst.
+
+### [P2] There is a missing live fan-out path: batch undo at `1933-1936`
+
+- `startUndoWindow` creates an `onUndo` callback at `1920-1941`
+- inside it, `1933-1936` loops `snapshots.forEach(...)` and calls `advanceMutation.mutate(...)` once per order
+
+This is not the reported S270 repro, but it is a real live batch-update path with the same N-mutation shape. If the prompt claims to fix the batch-rate-limit pattern generally, omitting undo leaves one burst path intact.
+
+### [P2] `handleCloseAllOrders` is a real hotspot, but it is not the reported repro path
+
+- `4122-4143`: `handleCloseAllOrders`
+- `4132-4133`: `await Promise.all(orders.map(o => base44.entities.Order.update(...)))`
+- `2131`: `handleCloseTableClick` only falls back to `onCloseAllOrders(group.orders)` when there is no `sessionId` / no close-table handler
+
+This is a valid batch hardening target, but the specific S270 reproduction in `BUGS.md` is "Выдать все" on 4 dishes, which maps more directly to:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` -> `1956-1965`
+
+### [P2] `120ms` is a heuristic, not a validated sufficiency threshold
+
+- default polling is `5000ms` at `508`
+- active queries refetch on that interval at `3449-3485`
+
+A serial batch plus single invalidation is the important fix. `120ms` may help smooth bursts, but static review cannot prove it is sufficient for the backend's real limit window. For 4 items it is likely fine if requests are truly serialized; for 10-30 item restaurant batches, polling can still overlap a long-running batch.
+
+Prompt guidance should therefore say:
+
+- use a named constant, not a magic number
+- treat the delay as tunable
+- do not claim "`120ms` is sufficient" as a fact unless it was tested
+
+## Direct answers
+
+### 1. Are all 5 fan-out locations correctly identified with right line numbers?
+
+If the draft's 5 locations are these live user-facing batch entry points, then the anchors are real:
+
+- `2333`: bulk request bar (`tableRequests.forEach(...)`)
+- `2335`: bulk `newOrders` button
+- `2337`: bulk `inProgressSections` button
+- `2339`: bulk `readyOrders` button
+- `4132-4133`: `Promise.all(...)` inside `handleCloseAllOrders`
+
+But two corrections are needed:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` are entry points, not the actual order fan-out loop. The real mutation fan-out is `1956-1965`.
+- If the draft cites `639` or `1254` for request bulk fan-out, those are wrong because both are inside commented code.
+
+### 2. Is `runBatchSequential` helper correct?
+
+Conceptually yes, but only if all of these are true:
+
+- it is promise-based and truly serial: `await` one item before starting the next
+- it works with `mutateAsync(...)` or direct entity-update promises, never `mutate(...)`
+- it delays only between items, not before the first or after the last
+- it fails fast and rethrows, rather than swallowing errors and continuing blindly
+
+Recommended shape:
+
+```js
+const BATCH_DELAY_MS = 120;
+
+const sleep = (ms) => new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
+
+async function runBatchSequential(items, task, delayMs = BATCH_DELAY_MS) {
+  for (let i = 0; i < items.length; i += 1) {
+    await task(items[i], i);
+    if (delayMs > 0 && i < items.length - 1) {
+      await sleep(delayMs);
+    }
+  }
+}
+```
+
+### 3. Is the invalidate-once optimization sound?
+
+Not by itself. It is only sound if the prompt also suppresses the existing per-mutation invalidations during batch mode:
+
+- orders: `1882-1897`
+- requests: `3513-3521`
+
+Without that, `mutateAsync` will still trigger `invalidateQueries(...)` once per item.
+
+### 4. Is `120ms` delay sufficient?
+
+Not something static review can certify. The prompt can justify `120ms` as a starting throttle value, but not as a proven-safe number. The safer statement is:
+
+- sequentialization is mandatory
+- single final invalidation is mandatory
+- `120ms` is a tunable starting point
+- if large batches still hit the backend limit, increase the delay and/or pause polling during batch
+
+### 5. Any missing fan-out locations?
+
+Yes.
+
+- Missing live order fan-out implementation site: `1956-1965`
+  - this is the one the three live bulk order buttons actually use
+- Missing live undo fan-out: `1933-1936`
+
+Potentially misleading non-live sites that should **not** be counted:
+
+- `639`
+- `1254`
+- `671`, `694`, `709`
+- `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+Those all sit inside commented snapshots.
+
+### 6. Is `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` change safe?
+
+Not as a blanket replacement at `4399`.
+
+It is safe only if the prompt also requires one of these:
+
+- every async caller `await`s it in `try/catch`
+- or every fire-and-forget caller uses `void onCloseRequestAsync(...).catch(...)`
+- or single-request buttons keep using sync `mutate(...)`, while bulk request paths use a separate async batch helper
+
+Without that, failures from request updates can escape as unhandled promise rejections.
+
+## Bottom line
+
+The prompt's main idea is good, but it is not implementation-safe unless it is tightened in four places:
+
+1. distinguish live fan-out code from commented duplicates
+2. target the real shared order batch loop at `1956-1965`
+3. explicitly suppress per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`
+4. do not globally replace `onCloseRequest` with `mutateAsync` without caller-side error handling or a separate async batch wrapper

+# Review: SOM-BUG-S270-01 KS Prompt
+
+Date: 2026-04-14
+Target: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx` (4538 lines)
+Context: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/BUGS.md`
+
+## Scope note
+
+I did not find a separate raw prompt file in the repository. This review validates the draft proposal as described by these checks:
+
+1. 5 fan-out locations
+2. `runBatchSequential` helper
+3. invalidate-once optimization
+4. `120ms` delay
+5. missing fan-out locations
+6. `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync`
+
+## Summary
+
+The draft direction is mostly right at the problem level: the current file does have real burst-update paths, and the reported `429` after "Выдать все" is credible from the live code. The main prompt risk is implementation precision. In this file, some candidate anchors are dead commented code, the actual order fan-out is centralized in one shared helper, and `mutateAsync` alone does not remove per-item invalidations because the mutation callbacks still fire on every call.
+
+## Findings
+
+### [P1] Invalidate-once is not sound if the prompt only switches loops to `mutateAsync`
+
+- `advanceMutation` still invalidates on every mutation settle at `1882-1897`:
+  - `1895`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["orders"] });`
+  - `1896`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["servedOrders", group.id] });`
+- `updateRequestMutation` still invalidates on every success at `3513-3521`:
+  - `3515`: `onSuccess: () => queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["serviceRequests"] }),`
+- `mutateAsync()` changes call shape, not mutation lifecycle. If the prompt says "use `mutateAsync` sequentially, then invalidate once after the loop", that is incomplete. The per-item `onSettled` / `onSuccess` handlers will still refetch unless the mutation callbacks are taught to skip invalidation during batch mode.
+
+Additional request-specific caveat:
+
+- `updateRequestMutation.mutationFn` currently spreads every non-`id` field into the entity update at `3514`.
+- Any batch-only flag such as `skipInvalidate`, `batch`, or `silent` would be written into `ServiceRequest` unless explicitly stripped there.
+
+### [P1] Global `onCloseRequest: mutate -> mutateAsync` is not a drop-in safe change
+
+- Parent wiring is currently synchronous at `4399`:
+  - `onCloseRequest={(reqId, newStatus, extraFields) => updateRequestMutation.mutate({ id: reqId, status: newStatus, ...extraFields })}`
+- Single-row request buttons call `onCloseRequest(...)` without awaiting or catching:
+  - live detail-view request actions are embedded on `2333`
+  - older mirrors at `658` and `1273` are inside block comments, not live
+- If `4399` is changed to `mutateAsync(...)`, those handlers start returning promises. On failure, that can produce unhandled promise rejections unless every caller does `await` with `try/catch`, or explicitly uses `void ...catch(...)`.
+
+Safer prompt direction:
+
+- keep the existing sync `onCloseRequest` for one-off button clicks
+- add a separate async batch-specific helper / prop for bulk request actions
+
+### [P1] The prompt must distinguish live fan-out points from dead commented duplicates
+
+There are two large commented-out render snapshots:
+
+- `546-785`
+- `1148-1418`
+
+That matters because several older bulk-action anchors inside those blocks are not live:
+
+- request bulk bar at `639`
+- request bulk bar at `1254`
+- bulk order buttons at `671`, `694`, `709`, `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+The only live request bulk fan-out is the detail-view bulk bar embedded on `2333`, where:
+
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "accept all"
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "serve all"
+
+### [P2] The real order fan-out is centralized at `1956-1965`, not at the three bulk button lines
+
+Live table-card bulk entry points are real:
+
+- `2335`: bulk action for `newOrders`
+- `2337`: bulk action for `inProgressSections`
+- `2339`: bulk action for `readyOrders`
+
+But those three buttons all funnel into one actual mutation fan-out:
+
+- `1956-1965`: `handleOrdersAction`
+- `1960-1962`: `actionable.forEach(... advanceMutation.mutate(...))`
+
+If the prompt only lists `2335/2337/2339`, the implementor can easily patch button call sites and miss the shared loop that actually creates the burst.
+
+### [P2] There is a missing live fan-out path: batch undo at `1933-1936`
+
+- `startUndoWindow` creates an `onUndo` callback at `1920-1941`
+- inside it, `1933-1936` loops `snapshots.forEach(...)` and calls `advanceMutation.mutate(...)` once per order
+
+This is not the reported S270 repro, but it is a real live batch-update path with the same N-mutation shape. If the prompt claims to fix the batch-rate-limit pattern generally, omitting undo leaves one burst path intact.
+
+### [P2] `handleCloseAllOrders` is a real hotspot, but it is not the reported repro path
+
+- `4122-4143`: `handleCloseAllOrders`
+- `4132-4133`: `await Promise.all(orders.map(o => base44.entities.Order.update(...)))`
+- `2131`: `handleCloseTableClick` only falls back to `onCloseAllOrders(group.orders)` when there is no `sessionId` / no close-table handler
+
+This is a valid batch hardening target, but the specific S270 reproduction in `BUGS.md` is "Выдать все" on 4 dishes, which maps more directly to:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` -> `1956-1965`
+
+### [P2] `120ms` is a heuristic, not a validated sufficiency threshold
+
+- default polling is `5000ms` at `508`
+- active queries refetch on that interval at `3449-3485`
+
+A serial batch plus single invalidation is the important fix. `120ms` may help smooth bursts, but static review cannot prove it is sufficient for the backend's real limit window. For 4 items it is likely fine if requests are truly serialized; for 10-30 item restaurant batches, polling can still overlap a long-running batch.
+
+Prompt guidance should therefore say:
+
+- use a named constant, not a magic number
+- treat the delay as tunable
+- do not claim "`120ms` is sufficient" as a fact unless it was tested
+
+## Direct answers
+
+### 1. Are all 5 fan-out locations correctly identified with right line numbers?
+
+If the draft's 5 locations are these live user-facing batch entry points, then the anchors are real:
+
+- `2333`: bulk request bar (`tableRequests.forEach(...)`)
+- `2335`: bulk `newOrders` button
+- `2337`: bulk `inProgressSections` button
+- `2339`: bulk `readyOrders` button
+- `4132-4133`: `Promise.all(...)` inside `handleCloseAllOrders`
+
+But two corrections are needed:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` are entry points, not the actual order fan-out loop. The real mutation fan-out is `1956-1965`.
+- If the draft cites `639` or `1254` for request bulk fan-out, those are wrong because both are inside commented code.
+
+### 2. Is `runBatchSequential` helper correct?
+
+Conceptually yes, but only if all of these are true:
+
+- it is promise-based and truly serial: `await` one item before starting the next
+- it works with `mutateAsync(...)` or direct entity-update promises, never `mutate(...)`
+- it delays only between items, not before the first or after the last
+- it fails fast and rethrows, rather than swallowing errors and continuing blindly
+
+Recommended shape:
+
+```js
+const BATCH_DELAY_MS = 120;
+
+const sleep = (ms) => new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
+
+async function runBatchSequential(items, task, delayMs = BATCH_DELAY_MS) {
+  for (let i = 0; i < items.length; i += 1) {
+    await task(items[i], i);
+    if (delayMs > 0 && i < items.length - 1) {
+      await sleep(delayMs);
+    }
+  }
+}
+```
+
+### 3. Is the invalidate-once optimization sound?
+
+Not by itself. It is only sound if the prompt also suppresses the existing per-mutation invalidations during batch mode:
+
+- orders: `1882-1897`
+- requests: `3513-3521`
+
+Without that, `mutateAsync` will still trigger `invalidateQueries(...)` once per item.
+
+### 4. Is `120ms` delay sufficient?
+
+Not something static review can certify. The prompt can justify `120ms` as a starting throttle value, but not as a proven-safe number. The safer statement is:
+
+- sequentialization is mandatory
+- single final invalidation is mandatory
+- `120ms` is a tunable starting point
+- if large batches still hit the backend limit, increase the delay and/or pause polling during batch
+
+### 5. Any missing fan-out locations?
+
+Yes.
+
+- Missing live order fan-out implementation site: `1956-1965`
+  - this is the one the three live bulk order buttons actually use
+- Missing live undo fan-out: `1933-1936`
+
+Potentially misleading non-live sites that should **not** be counted:
+
+- `639`
+- `1254`
+- `671`, `694`, `709`
+- `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+Those all sit inside commented snapshots.
+
+### 6. Is `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` change safe?
+
+Not as a blanket replacement at `4399`.
+
+It is safe only if the prompt also requires one of these:
+
+- every async caller `await`s it in `try/catch`
+- or every fire-and-forget caller uses `void onCloseRequestAsync(...).catch(...)`
+- or single-request buttons keep using sync `mutate(...)`, while bulk request paths use a separate async batch helper
+
+Without that, failures from request updates can escape as unhandled promise rejections.
+
+## Bottom line
+
+The prompt's main idea is good, but it is not implementation-safe unless it is tightened in four places:
+
+1. distinguish live fan-out code from commented duplicates
+2. target the real shared order batch loop at `1956-1965`
+3. explicitly suppress per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`
+4. do not globally replace `onCloseRequest` with `mutateAsync` without caller-side error handling or a separate async batch wrapper

The review is complete and the report plus command log have been saved in the StaffOrdersMobile page folder.

  ✓ Evaluate the proposed fixes: sequential batching helper, single invalidation, delay sizing, and mutateAsync safety
  ✓ Write the review report and commands log into pages/StaffOrdersMobile

+# Review: SOM-BUG-S270-01 KS Prompt
+
+Date: 2026-04-14
+Target: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx` (4538 lines)
+Context: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/BUGS.md`
+
+## Scope note
+
+I did not find a separate raw prompt file in the repository. This review validates the draft proposal as described by these checks:
+
+1. 5 fan-out locations
+2. `runBatchSequential` helper
+3. invalidate-once optimization
+4. `120ms` delay
+5. missing fan-out locations
+6. `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync`
+
+## Summary
+
+The draft direction is mostly right at the problem level: the current file does have real burst-update paths, and the reported `429` after "Выдать все" is credible from the live code. The main prompt risk is implementation precision. In this file, some candidate anchors are dead commented code, the actual order fan-out is centralized in one shared helper, and `mutateAsync` alone does not remove per-item invalidations because the mutation callbacks still fire on every call.
+
+## Findings
+
+### [P1] Invalidate-once is not sound if the prompt only switches loops to `mutateAsync`
+
+- `advanceMutation` still invalidates on every mutation settle at `1882-1897`:
+  - `1895`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["orders"] });`
+  - `1896`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["servedOrders", group.id] });`
+- `updateRequestMutation` still invalidates on every success at `3513-3521`:
+  - `3515`: `onSuccess: () => queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["serviceRequests"] }),`
+- `mutateAsync()` changes call shape, not mutation lifecycle. If the prompt says "use `mutateAsync` sequentially, then invalidate once after the loop", that is incomplete. The per-item `onSettled` / `onSuccess` handlers will still refetch unless the mutation callbacks are taught to skip invalidation during batch mode.
+
+Additional request-specific caveat:
+
+- `updateRequestMutation.mutationFn` currently spreads every non-`id` field into the entity update at `3514`.
+- Any batch-only flag such as `skipInvalidate`, `batch`, or `silent` would be written into `ServiceRequest` unless explicitly stripped there.
+
+### [P1] Global `onCloseRequest: mutate -> mutateAsync` is not a drop-in safe change
+
+- Parent wiring is currently synchronous at `4399`:
+  - `onCloseRequest={(reqId, newStatus, extraFields) => updateRequestMutation.mutate({ id: reqId, status: newStatus, ...extraFields })}`
+- Single-row request buttons call `onCloseRequest(...)` without awaiting or catching:
+  - live detail-view request actions are embedded on `2333`
+  - older mirrors at `658` and `1273` are inside block comments, not live
+- If `4399` is changed to `mutateAsync(...)`, those handlers start returning promises. On failure, that can produce unhandled promise rejections unless every caller does `await` with `try/catch`, or explicitly uses `void ...catch(...)`.
+
+Safer prompt direction:
+
+- keep the existing sync `onCloseRequest` for one-off button clicks
+- add a separate async batch-specific helper / prop for bulk request actions
+
+### [P1] The prompt must distinguish live fan-out points from dead commented duplicates
+
+There are two large commented-out render snapshots:
+
+- `546-785`
+- `1148-1418`
+
+That matters because several older bulk-action anchors inside those blocks are not live:
+
+- request bulk bar at `639`
+- request bulk bar at `1254`
+- bulk order buttons at `671`, `694`, `709`, `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+The only live request bulk fan-out is the detail-view bulk bar embedded on `2333`, where:
+
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "accept all"
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "serve all"
+
+### [P2] The real order fan-out is centralized at `1956-1965`, not at the three bulk button lines
+
+Live table-card bulk entry points are real:
+
+- `2335`: bulk action for `newOrders`
+- `2337`: bulk action for `inProgressSections`
+- `2339`: bulk action for `readyOrders`
+
+But those three buttons all funnel into one actual mutation fan-out:
+
+- `1956-1965`: `handleOrdersAction`
+- `1960-1962`: `actionable.forEach(... advanceMutation.mutate(...))`
+
+If the prompt only lists `2335/2337/2339`, the implementor can easily patch button call sites and miss the shared loop that actually creates the burst.
+
+### [P2] There is a missing live fan-out path: batch undo at `1933-1936`
+
+- `startUndoWindow` creates an `onUndo` callback at `1920-1941`
+- inside it, `1933-1936` loops `snapshots.forEach(...)` and calls `advanceMutation.mutate(...)` once per order
+
+This is not the reported S270 repro, but it is a real live batch-update path with the same N-mutation shape. If the prompt claims to fix the batch-rate-limit pattern generally, omitting undo leaves one burst path intact.
+
+### [P2] `handleCloseAllOrders` is a real hotspot, but it is not the reported repro path
+
+- `4122-4143`: `handleCloseAllOrders`
+- `4132-4133`: `await Promise.all(orders.map(o => base44.entities.Order.update(...)))`
+- `2131`: `handleCloseTableClick` only falls back to `onCloseAllOrders(group.orders)` when there is no `sessionId` / no close-table handler
+
+This is a valid batch hardening target, but the specific S270 reproduction in `BUGS.md` is "Выдать все" on 4 dishes, which maps more directly to:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` -> `1956-1965`
+
+### [P2] `120ms` is a heuristic, not a validated sufficiency threshold
+
+- default polling is `5000ms` at `508`
+- active queries refetch on that interval at `3449-3485`
+
+A serial batch plus single invalidation is the important fix. `120ms` may help smooth bursts, but static review cannot prove it is sufficient for the backend's real limit window. For 4 items it is likely fine if requests are truly serialized; for 10-30 item restaurant batches, polling can still overlap a long-running batch.
+
+Prompt guidance should therefore say:
+
+- use a named constant, not a magic number
+- treat the delay as tunable
+- do not claim "`120ms` is sufficient" as a fact unless it was tested
+
+## Direct answers
+
+### 1. Are all 5 fan-out locations correctly identified with right line numbers?
+
+If the draft's 5 locations are these live user-facing batch entry points, then the anchors are real:
+
+- `2333`: bulk request bar (`tableRequests.forEach(...)`)
+- `2335`: bulk `newOrders` button
+- `2337`: bulk `inProgressSections` button
+- `2339`: bulk `readyOrders` button
+- `4132-4133`: `Promise.all(...)` inside `handleCloseAllOrders`
+
+But two corrections are needed:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` are entry points, not the actual order fan-out loop. The real mutation fan-out is `1956-1965`.
+- If the draft cites `639` or `1254` for request bulk fan-out, those are wrong because both are inside commented code.
+
+### 2. Is `runBatchSequential` helper correct?
+
+Conceptually yes, but only if all of these are true:
+
+- it is promise-based and truly serial: `await` one item before starting the next
+- it works with `mutateAsync(...)` or direct entity-update promises, never `mutate(...)`
+- it delays only between items, not before the first or after the last
+- it fails fast and rethrows, rather than swallowing errors and continuing blindly
+
+Recommended shape:
+
+```js
+const BATCH_DELAY_MS = 120;
+
+const sleep = (ms) => new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
+
+async function runBatchSequential(items, task, delayMs = BATCH_DELAY_MS) {
+  for (let i = 0; i < items.length; i += 1) {
+    await task(items[i], i);
+    if (delayMs > 0 && i < items.length - 1) {
+      await sleep(delayMs);
+    }
+  }
+}
+```
+
+### 3. Is the invalidate-once optimization sound?
+
+Not by itself. It is only sound if the prompt also suppresses the existing per-mutation invalidations during batch mode:
+
+- orders: `1882-1897`
+- requests: `3513-3521`
+
+Without that, `mutateAsync` will still trigger `invalidateQueries(...)` once per item.
+
+### 4. Is `120ms` delay sufficient?
+
+Not something static review can certify. The prompt can justify `120ms` as a starting throttle value, but not as a proven-safe number. The safer statement is:
+
+- sequentialization is mandatory
+- single final invalidation is mandatory
+- `120ms` is a tunable starting point
+- if large batches still hit the backend limit, increase the delay and/or pause polling during batch
+
+### 5. Any missing fan-out locations?
+
+Yes.
+
+- Missing live order fan-out implementation site: `1956-1965`
+  - this is the one the three live bulk order buttons actually use
+- Missing live undo fan-out: `1933-1936`
+
+Potentially misleading non-live sites that should **not** be counted:
+
+- `639`
+- `1254`
+- `671`, `694`, `709`
+- `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+Those all sit inside commented snapshots.
+
+### 6. Is `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` change safe?
+
+Not as a blanket replacement at `4399`.
+
+It is safe only if the prompt also requires one of these:
+
+- every async caller `await`s it in `try/catch`
+- or every fire-and-forget caller uses `void onCloseRequestAsync(...).catch(...)`
+- or single-request buttons keep using sync `mutate(...)`, while bulk request paths use a separate async batch helper
+
+Without that, failures from request updates can escape as unhandled promise rejections.
+
+## Bottom line
+
+The prompt's main idea is good, but it is not implementation-safe unless it is tightened in four places:
+
+1. distinguish live fan-out code from commented duplicates
+2. target the real shared order batch loop at `1956-1965`
+3. explicitly suppress per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`
+4. do not globally replace `onCloseRequest` with `mutateAsync` without caller-side error handling or a separate async batch wrapper

codex
The prompt’s weakest point is the invalidate-once story. In the live file, `mutateAsync` alone will not reduce invalidations to one: `advanceMutation.onSettled` still invalidates per item at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:1882>) and `updateRequestMutation.onSuccess` still invalidates per item at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:3513>). For requests, any batch-only flag also has to be stripped in the mutation function at line 3514, otherwise it gets passed into `ServiceRequest.update(...)`.

The other prompt-level risk is the proposed `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync` swap. As a blanket change at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:4399>) it is not drop-in safe, because the live request buttons in the detail view call `onCloseRequest(...)` fire-and-forget at line 2333. If that starts returning rejecting promises, failures can surface as unhandled promise rejections unless every caller `await`s or catches them.

Direct answers:

1. If the prompt’s “5 fan-out locations” are the live entry points at `2333`, `2335`, `2337`, `2339`, and `4132-4133`, those anchors are real. But `2335/2337/2339` are only UI entry points; the actual shared order fan-out happens once in `handleOrdersAction` at `1956-1965`.
2. `runBatchSequential` is conceptually correct only if it is truly serial, uses `mutateAsync` or direct entity-update promises, delays between items only, and rethrows on error. If it wraps `mutate(...)`, it is not correct.
3. The invalidate-once optimization is not sound unless the prompt also suppresses the existing per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`.
4. `120ms` is a heuristic, not something static review can certify as sufficient. The real fix is serialization plus single final invalidation. With default 5s polling at `508` and `3449-3485`, long batches can still overlap a refetch.
5. Yes, there is a missing live fan-out location: undo batch at `1933-1936`. Also, if the prompt does not cite `1956-1965`, it is missing the real shared order batch loop.
6. `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` is only safe if the async callers `await` it in `try/catch`, or fire-and-forget callers explicitly `.catch(...)`. Safer prompt design: keep the sync single-item path and add a separate async batch helper for bulk requests.

One more important precision point: only the bulk request bar at line `2333` is live. Older copies at `639` and `1254` are inside block comments (`546-785` and `1148-1418`) and should not be counted as current fan-out locations.

+# Review: SOM-BUG-S270-01 KS Prompt
+
+Date: 2026-04-14
+Target: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx` (4538 lines)
+Context: `pages/StaffOrdersMobile/BUGS.md`
+
+## Scope note
+
+I did not find a separate raw prompt file in the repository. This review validates the draft proposal as described by these checks:
+
+1. 5 fan-out locations
+2. `runBatchSequential` helper
+3. invalidate-once optimization
+4. `120ms` delay
+5. missing fan-out locations
+6. `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync`
+
+## Summary
+
+The draft direction is mostly right at the problem level: the current file does have real burst-update paths, and the reported `429` after "Выдать все" is credible from the live code. The main prompt risk is implementation precision. In this file, some candidate anchors are dead commented code, the actual order fan-out is centralized in one shared helper, and `mutateAsync` alone does not remove per-item invalidations because the mutation callbacks still fire on every call.
+
+## Findings
+
+### [P1] Invalidate-once is not sound if the prompt only switches loops to `mutateAsync`
+
+- `advanceMutation` still invalidates on every mutation settle at `1882-1897`:
+  - `1895`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["orders"] });`
+  - `1896`: `queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["servedOrders", group.id] });`
+- `updateRequestMutation` still invalidates on every success at `3513-3521`:
+  - `3515`: `onSuccess: () => queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["serviceRequests"] }),`
+- `mutateAsync()` changes call shape, not mutation lifecycle. If the prompt says "use `mutateAsync` sequentially, then invalidate once after the loop", that is incomplete. The per-item `onSettled` / `onSuccess` handlers will still refetch unless the mutation callbacks are taught to skip invalidation during batch mode.
+
+Additional request-specific caveat:
+
+- `updateRequestMutation.mutationFn` currently spreads every non-`id` field into the entity update at `3514`.
+- Any batch-only flag such as `skipInvalidate`, `batch`, or `silent` would be written into `ServiceRequest` unless explicitly stripped there.
+
+### [P1] Global `onCloseRequest: mutate -> mutateAsync` is not a drop-in safe change
+
+- Parent wiring is currently synchronous at `4399`:
+  - `onCloseRequest={(reqId, newStatus, extraFields) => updateRequestMutation.mutate({ id: reqId, status: newStatus, ...extraFields })}`
+- Single-row request buttons call `onCloseRequest(...)` without awaiting or catching:
+  - live detail-view request actions are embedded on `2333`
+  - older mirrors at `658` and `1273` are inside block comments, not live
+- If `4399` is changed to `mutateAsync(...)`, those handlers start returning promises. On failure, that can produce unhandled promise rejections unless every caller does `await` with `try/catch`, or explicitly uses `void ...catch(...)`.
+
+Safer prompt direction:
+
+- keep the existing sync `onCloseRequest` for one-off button clicks
+- add a separate async batch-specific helper / prop for bulk request actions
+
+### [P1] The prompt must distinguish live fan-out points from dead commented duplicates
+
+There are two large commented-out render snapshots:
+
+- `546-785`
+- `1148-1418`
+
+That matters because several older bulk-action anchors inside those blocks are not live:
+
+- request bulk bar at `639`
+- request bulk bar at `1254`
+- bulk order buttons at `671`, `694`, `709`, `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+The only live request bulk fan-out is the detail-view bulk bar embedded on `2333`, where:
+
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "accept all"
+- `tableRequests.forEach(r => onCloseRequest(...))` handles "serve all"
+
+### [P2] The real order fan-out is centralized at `1956-1965`, not at the three bulk button lines
+
+Live table-card bulk entry points are real:
+
+- `2335`: bulk action for `newOrders`
+- `2337`: bulk action for `inProgressSections`
+- `2339`: bulk action for `readyOrders`
+
+But those three buttons all funnel into one actual mutation fan-out:
+
+- `1956-1965`: `handleOrdersAction`
+- `1960-1962`: `actionable.forEach(... advanceMutation.mutate(...))`
+
+If the prompt only lists `2335/2337/2339`, the implementor can easily patch button call sites and miss the shared loop that actually creates the burst.
+
+### [P2] There is a missing live fan-out path: batch undo at `1933-1936`
+
+- `startUndoWindow` creates an `onUndo` callback at `1920-1941`
+- inside it, `1933-1936` loops `snapshots.forEach(...)` and calls `advanceMutation.mutate(...)` once per order
+
+This is not the reported S270 repro, but it is a real live batch-update path with the same N-mutation shape. If the prompt claims to fix the batch-rate-limit pattern generally, omitting undo leaves one burst path intact.
+
+### [P2] `handleCloseAllOrders` is a real hotspot, but it is not the reported repro path
+
+- `4122-4143`: `handleCloseAllOrders`
+- `4132-4133`: `await Promise.all(orders.map(o => base44.entities.Order.update(...)))`
+- `2131`: `handleCloseTableClick` only falls back to `onCloseAllOrders(group.orders)` when there is no `sessionId` / no close-table handler
+
+This is a valid batch hardening target, but the specific S270 reproduction in `BUGS.md` is "Выдать все" on 4 dishes, which maps more directly to:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` -> `1956-1965`
+
+### [P2] `120ms` is a heuristic, not a validated sufficiency threshold
+
+- default polling is `5000ms` at `508`
+- active queries refetch on that interval at `3449-3485`
+
+A serial batch plus single invalidation is the important fix. `120ms` may help smooth bursts, but static review cannot prove it is sufficient for the backend's real limit window. For 4 items it is likely fine if requests are truly serialized; for 10-30 item restaurant batches, polling can still overlap a long-running batch.
+
+Prompt guidance should therefore say:
+
+- use a named constant, not a magic number
+- treat the delay as tunable
+- do not claim "`120ms` is sufficient" as a fact unless it was tested
+
+## Direct answers
+
+### 1. Are all 5 fan-out locations correctly identified with right line numbers?
+
+If the draft's 5 locations are these live user-facing batch entry points, then the anchors are real:
+
+- `2333`: bulk request bar (`tableRequests.forEach(...)`)
+- `2335`: bulk `newOrders` button
+- `2337`: bulk `inProgressSections` button
+- `2339`: bulk `readyOrders` button
+- `4132-4133`: `Promise.all(...)` inside `handleCloseAllOrders`
+
+But two corrections are needed:
+
+- `2335/2337/2339` are entry points, not the actual order fan-out loop. The real mutation fan-out is `1956-1965`.
+- If the draft cites `639` or `1254` for request bulk fan-out, those are wrong because both are inside commented code.
+
+### 2. Is `runBatchSequential` helper correct?
+
+Conceptually yes, but only if all of these are true:
+
+- it is promise-based and truly serial: `await` one item before starting the next
+- it works with `mutateAsync(...)` or direct entity-update promises, never `mutate(...)`
+- it delays only between items, not before the first or after the last
+- it fails fast and rethrows, rather than swallowing errors and continuing blindly
+
+Recommended shape:
+
+```js
+const BATCH_DELAY_MS = 120;
+
+const sleep = (ms) => new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
+
+async function runBatchSequential(items, task, delayMs = BATCH_DELAY_MS) {
+  for (let i = 0; i < items.length; i += 1) {
+    await task(items[i], i);
+    if (delayMs > 0 && i < items.length - 1) {
+      await sleep(delayMs);
+    }
+  }
+}
+```
+
+### 3. Is the invalidate-once optimization sound?
+
+Not by itself. It is only sound if the prompt also suppresses the existing per-mutation invalidations during batch mode:
+
+- orders: `1882-1897`
+- requests: `3513-3521`
+
+Without that, `mutateAsync` will still trigger `invalidateQueries(...)` once per item.
+
+### 4. Is `120ms` delay sufficient?
+
+Not something static review can certify. The prompt can justify `120ms` as a starting throttle value, but not as a proven-safe number. The safer statement is:
+
+- sequentialization is mandatory
+- single final invalidation is mandatory
+- `120ms` is a tunable starting point
+- if large batches still hit the backend limit, increase the delay and/or pause polling during batch
+
+### 5. Any missing fan-out locations?
+
+Yes.
+
+- Missing live order fan-out implementation site: `1956-1965`
+  - this is the one the three live bulk order buttons actually use
+- Missing live undo fan-out: `1933-1936`
+
+Potentially misleading non-live sites that should **not** be counted:
+
+- `639`
+- `1254`
+- `671`, `694`, `709`
+- `1286`, `1309`, `1324`
+
+Those all sit inside commented snapshots.
+
+### 6. Is `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` change safe?
+
+Not as a blanket replacement at `4399`.
+
+It is safe only if the prompt also requires one of these:
+
+- every async caller `await`s it in `try/catch`
+- or every fire-and-forget caller uses `void onCloseRequestAsync(...).catch(...)`
+- or single-request buttons keep using sync `mutate(...)`, while bulk request paths use a separate async batch helper
+
+Without that, failures from request updates can escape as unhandled promise rejections.
+
+## Bottom line
+
+The prompt's main idea is good, but it is not implementation-safe unless it is tightened in four places:
+
+1. distinguish live fan-out code from commented duplicates
+2. target the real shared order batch loop at `1956-1965`
+3. explicitly suppress per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`
+4. do not globally replace `onCloseRequest` with `mutateAsync` without caller-side error handling or a separate async batch wrapper

The prompt’s weakest point is the invalidate-once story. In the live file, `mutateAsync` alone will not reduce invalidations to one: `advanceMutation.onSettled` still invalidates per item at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:1882>) and `updateRequestMutation.onSuccess` still invalidates per item at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:3513>). For requests, any batch-only flag also has to be stripped in the mutation function at line 3514, otherwise it gets passed into `ServiceRequest.update(...)`.

The other prompt-level risk is the proposed `onCloseRequest` `mutate -> mutateAsync` swap. As a blanket change at [260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx](</C:/Dev/menuapp-code-review/pages/StaffOrdersMobile/260414-01 StaffOrdersMobile RELEASE.jsx:4399>) it is not drop-in safe, because the live request buttons in the detail view call `onCloseRequest(...)` fire-and-forget at line 2333. If that starts returning rejecting promises, failures can surface as unhandled promise rejections unless every caller `await`s or catches them.

Direct answers:

1. If the prompt’s “5 fan-out locations” are the live entry points at `2333`, `2335`, `2337`, `2339`, and `4132-4133`, those anchors are real. But `2335/2337/2339` are only UI entry points; the actual shared order fan-out happens once in `handleOrdersAction` at `1956-1965`.
2. `runBatchSequential` is conceptually correct only if it is truly serial, uses `mutateAsync` or direct entity-update promises, delays between items only, and rethrows on error. If it wraps `mutate(...)`, it is not correct.
3. The invalidate-once optimization is not sound unless the prompt also suppresses the existing per-item invalidations in `1882-1897` and `3513-3521`.
4. `120ms` is a heuristic, not something static review can certify as sufficient. The real fix is serialization plus single final invalidation. With default 5s polling at `508` and `3449-3485`, long batches can still overlap a refetch.
5. Yes, there is a missing live fan-out location: undo batch at `1933-1936`. Also, if the prompt does not cite `1956-1965`, it is missing the real shared order batch loop.
6. `onCloseRequest mutate -> mutateAsync` is only safe if the async callers `await` it in `try/catch`, or fire-and-forget callers explicitly `.catch(...)`. Safer prompt design: keep the sync single-item path and add a separate async batch helper for bulk requests.

One more important precision point: only the bulk request bar at line `2333` is live. Older copies at `639` and `1254` are inside block comments (`546-785` and `1148-1418`) and should not be counted as current fan-out locations.
